# ( Include screenshot of transcript )

We have the option of retaining some of the HTML so we can determine actions, possibly better sentiment accuracy. For now we will just use text.

In [33]:
content = r.content
In [34]:
from bs4 import BeautifulSoup as bs
In [37]:
soup = bs(content, 'html.parser')

After looking through the soup, we find that the content is in a div class called "poem". We will need to later confirm that this is the same class div for all transcripts.

In [61]:
transcript = soup.find('div', {'class':'poem'})
In [62]:
transcript
Out[62]:

<p>[Open Mortys room]<br/>

on the lights.)<br/>
<b>Rick:</b> Morty! You gotta come on. Jus'... You gotta come with me.<br/>

<b>Rick:</b>I got a surprise for you, Morty.<br/>
<b>Morty:</b>It's the middle of the night. What are you talking about?<br/>
<b>Rick:</b>*spills booze on Morty's bed* Come on, I got a surprise for you. *drags Morty by the ankle* Come on,<br/>
hurry up.<br/>
(Rick pulls Morty out of his bed and into the hall.)<br/>

Oooookay. What do we want to do with this? The first thing that comes to mind is to see how many words are spoken per character - but first let's create that function to pull transcript content from a wiki page. To do this we'll start by simply copy-pasting what we've done so far in the cells above.

In [63]:
# given a url:
def get_transcript(url):
    r = requests.get(url)
    content = r.content
    soup = bs(content, 'html.parser')
    transcript = soup.find('div', {'class':'poem'})
    return transcript

We'll also save this function in a .py file so we can import it in another session. We'll save the transcript URLs for importing as well so we don't have to read a txt file.

In [70]:
from evilmorty import urls, get_transcript

for u in urls:
    try:
        get_transcript(u)
    except Exception:
        print(u, Exception)
In [71]:
test = urls[0]
transcript = get_transcript(test)
